</div>
			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of current heads of state and government</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div role="note" class="hatnote">"World leaders" redirects here. For the CIA-published public domain directory, see <a href="/wiki/World_Leaders" title="World Leaders">World Leaders</a>.</div>
<p>This is a <b>list of current heads of state and government</b>, showing <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">heads of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">heads of government</a> where different, mainly in <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary systems</a>. Often a leader is both in <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential systems</a>. Some states have <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential systems</a>, where the head of government role (i.e. executive branch) is fulfilled by both the listed head of government and head of state.</p>
<p>The list includes the names of recently elected or appointed heads who will take office on an appointed date.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Member_and_observer_states_of_the_United_Nations">Member and observer states of the United Nations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_current_heads_of_state_and_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Member and observer states of the United Nations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl>
<dd>
<dl>
<dt><i>Legend:</i></dt>
</dl>
</dd>
</dl>
<ul>
<li style="list-style-type: none; list-style-image: none; text-indent: -1.5em; margin: 0;"><span style="border-left: 1.2em solid; border-left-color: LightYellow; padding-left: 0.4em;" title="Farbe LightYellow">﻿</span><i>Yellow highlighted cells indicate state leaders whose constitutionally interpreted positions</i> (e.g. <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/de_jure" class="extiw" title="wikt:de jure">de jure</a></i>) <i>individually administer the <a href="/wiki/Government" title="Government">governmental</a> <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislature</a></i></li>
<li style="list-style-type: none; list-style-image: none; text-indent: -1.5em; margin: 0;"><span style="border-left: 1.2em solid; border-left-color: LightCyan; padding-left: 0.4em;" title="Farbe LightCyan">﻿</span><i>Blue highlighted cells distinguish heads of state or <a href="/wiki/Party_leader" title="Party leader">party leaders</a> chiefly regarded as exercising</i> (e.g. <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/de_facto" class="extiw" title="wikt:de facto">de facto</a></i>) <i>further systemic influence, authority within their <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_system_of_government" title="List of countries by system of government">system of government</a></i></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><i>Names in small font generally denote acting, transitional, temporary leaders, or representatives. Other notes and exceptions are provided at <a href="#Notes">§&#160;Notes</a>.</i></li>
</ul>

<td>
<div class="hlist inline">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_states">Other states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_current_heads_of_state_and_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Other states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The following states control their territory and are recognised by at least one <abbr title="United Nations">UN</abbr> member state.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<table class="wikitable plainrowheaders">
<tr>

<td><a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_Syrian_National_Coalition" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister of the Syrian National Coalition">Prime Minister</a>&#160;– <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jawad_Abu_Hatab&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jawad Abu Hatab (page does not exist)">Jawad Abu Hatab</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;(<a href="https://ar.wikipedia.org/wiki/%D8%AC%D9%88%D8%A7%D8%AF_%D8%A3%D8%A8%D9%88_%D8%AD%D8%B7%D8%A8" class="extiw" title="ar:جواد أبو حطب">ar</a>)</span></td>
</tr>
</table>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_current_heads_of_state_and_government&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-greek;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-WeakPM-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-7"><sup><i><b>h</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-8"><sup><i><b>i</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-9"><sup><i><b>j</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-10"><sup><i><b>k</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-11"><sup><i><b>l</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-12"><sup><i><b>m</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-13"><sup><i><b>n</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-14"><sup><i><b>o</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-15"><sup><i><b>p</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-16"><sup><i><b>q</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-17"><sup><i><b>r</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-18"><sup><i><b>s</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-19"><sup><i><b>t</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-20"><sup><i><b>u</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-21"><sup><i><b>v</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-22"><sup><i><b>w</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-WeakPM_1-23"><sup><i><b>x</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">In this state, the <a href="/wiki/President" title="President">president</a> is both head of state and government; the office of <a href="/wiki/Prime_minister" title="Prime minister">prime minister</a> may exist in these states, but it does not direct executive power (neither does the Afghan <a href="/wiki/Chief_Executive_Officer_(Afghanistan)" title="Chief Executive Officer (Afghanistan)">Chief Executive Officer</a>, nor the Burmese <a href="/wiki/State_Counsellor_of_Myanmar" title="State Counsellor of Myanmar">State Counsellor</a>, either).</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-FR-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-FR_2-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FR_2-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/President_of_France" title="President of France">President of France</a> and the French Co-Prince of Andorra are positions held by the same person.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-EIIR-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-EIIR_3-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-EIIR_3-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-EIIR_3-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-EIIR_3-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-EIIR_3-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-EIIR_3-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-EIIR_3-6"><sup><i><b>g</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-EIIR_3-7"><sup><i><b>h</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-EIIR_3-8"><sup><i><b>i</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-EIIR_3-9"><sup><i><b>j</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-EIIR_3-10"><sup><i><b>k</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-EIIR_3-11"><sup><i><b>l</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-EIIR_3-12"><sup><i><b>m</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-EIIR_3-13"><sup><i><b>n</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-EIIR_3-14"><sup><i><b>o</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-EIIR_3-15"><sup><i><b>p</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-EIIR_3-16"><sup><i><b>q</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-EIIR_3-17"><sup><i><b>r</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Constitutionally, Elizabeth is separately and equally monarch of 16 sovereign states (alongside the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>) known collectively as the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">Commonwealth realms</a>. In each of these states, with the exception of the UK (where she permanently resides) she is duly represented at the national level by a <a href="/wiki/Governor-general" title="Governor-general">governor-general</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-AT-4"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-AT_4-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The acting three-member Austrian Federal Presidential college (made up of the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_the_National_Council_of_Austria" class="mw-redirect" title="Presidency of the National Council of Austria">three Presidents</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Council_(Austria)" title="National Council (Austria)">National Council</a>) is a collective and temporary head of state.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-BA-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-BA_5-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The three-member Bosnian presidency is the head of state collectively.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-BR-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-BR_6-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Temer assumed the Brazilian presidential powers and duties during the course of the <a href="/wiki/Impeachment_of_Dilma_Rousseff" title="Impeachment of Dilma Rousseff">suspension</a> of Dilma Rousseff on 12 May. Temer assumed the presidency outright when Rousseff was impeached on 31 August.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-NZ-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-NZ_7-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-NZ_7-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The Governor-General of New Zealand and the <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_New_Zealand" title="Governor-General of New Zealand">Governor-General of Niue</a> are positions held by the same person.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-KP3-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-KP3_8-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The term "<a href="/wiki/Supreme_Leader" class="mw-redirect" title="Supreme Leader">Supreme Leader</a>" is used as a description (for the sake of brevity) rather than being an official title of a single office. The three actual offices held by Kim are:</span>
<ol>
<li><span class="reference-text">Chairman of the Workers' Party of Korea</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text">Chairman of the State Affairs Commission</span></li>
<li><span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Supreme_Commander_of_the_Korean_People%27s_Army" title="Supreme Commander of the Korean People's Army">Supreme Commander of the Korean People's Army</a></span></li>
</ol>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-KP4-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-KP4_9-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The President (otherwise known as Chairman) of the Presidium of the Supreme People's Assembly accepts the credentials of foreign ambassadors, signs treaties, receives visiting heads of state, and represents North Korea on all state visits (ceremonial functions usually performed by heads of state in other states). The president has held these duties since 1998, when the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_North_Korea" title="Constitution of North Korea">constitution</a> was revised.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-SM-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-SM_10-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Since 2012, the <a href="/wiki/Grand_and_General_Council" title="Grand and General Council">Grand and General Council</a> of San Marino has held a larger proportion of seats for the <a href="/wiki/Sammarinese_Christian_Democratic_Party" title="Sammarinese Christian Democratic Party">Christian Democratic Party</a> than those for the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Alliance_(San_Marino)" title="Popular Alliance (San Marino)">Popular Alliance</a>; it can thus be inferred that the partner belonging to the former party exercises wider legislative capabilities than the latter through its parliamentary superiority, outnumbering the latter party over 4,000 seats.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-CH-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-CH_11-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The seven-member Swiss Federal Council is head of state and government collectively. As a party to the Council, the president serves solely in a <i><a href="/wiki/Primus_inter_pares#Switzerland" title="Primus inter pares">primus inter pares</a></i> capacity for one year.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-TR-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-TR_12-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In theory, Erdoğan is barred from wielding political power (with the head of state constitutionally and legislatively bound to act within ceremonial capacity). Despite these legal constraints, Erdoğan has sought to preserve his persona as the paramount <a href="/wiki/Strongman_(politics)" title="Strongman (politics)">strongman</a> of Turkish politics, and is widely perceived by both the Turkish public and <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Turkey" title="Media of Turkey">media</a> in general as in practice the paramount leader of Turkey itself (notwithstanding his resignation as prime minister and election to the Turkish presidency). Moreover, considering the unconstitutional nature of these circumstances, constitutional experts<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (September 2016)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> have frequently referred to his persistent partisan leverage favouring the <a href="/wiki/Justice_and_Development_Party_(Turkey)" title="Justice and Development Party (Turkey)">Justice and Development Party</a> (AKP), the ruling party he founded and hitherto led, as the extended root of his political capital.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-FAS-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-FAS_13-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-FAS_13-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">States in <a href="/wiki/Associated_state" title="Associated state">free association</a> with New Zealand.</span></li>
</ol>
</div>
